# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Overview

**Task ID**: c_fintech_payment_expert_065_architectural_understanding_expert_01
**Category**: architectural_understanding
**Difficulty**: expert
**Language**: c
**Context Length**: 886345 tokens

## Task Title

Architectural Design for Cross-Service Tuition Auto-Payment

## Description

EduPay Ledger Academy is a sophisticated FinTech platform designed to manage all financial operations for a university. The system is built in C and employs a microservices architecture, with key services for the Bursar's Office (`bursar_service`) and the Financial Aid Office (`financial_aid_service`). The architecture heavily relies on advanced patterns including Clean Architecture, CQRS with Event Sourcing, and the Saga pattern for managing distributed transactions across services. A new feature is requested: 'Tuition Auto-Payment'. This feature should automatically apply a student's newly disbursed financial aid stipend towards their outstanding tuition balance, but only if the student has explicitly opted in. The challenge is to design a solution that seamlessly integrates this cross-service functionality while upholding the system's strict architectural principles of consistency, reliability, and regulatory compliance.

## Your Task

As a senior software architect for the EduPay Ledger Academy project, you are tasked with creating a detailed architectural proposal for the new 'Tuition Auto-Payment' feature. Your proposal should be a technical markdown document that outlines how to implement this feature without violating the existing architectural patterns.

Your proposal must address the following points:

1.  **Interaction Diagram/Sequence:** Describe the step-by-step flow of communication between the `financial_aid_service`, the `bursar_service`, and any other relevant components. Detail the sequence of commands, events, and queries.
2.  **Saga Pattern Integration:** Explain how the Saga pattern will be used to manage the distributed transaction. Will you extend an existing saga (like the one in `disburse_stipend_saga.c`) or create a new one? Justify your choice and describe the saga's steps, including any necessary compensating actions.
3.  **New Domain Events:** Define the new domain events required for this feature (e.g., for successful application, failure, etc.). Specify which service would publish these events and which services would consume them.
4.  **CQRS/Event Sourcing Impact:** Detail how this new workflow will be recorded in the event store. Explain which aggregates in the `bursar_service` (e.g., `Account`, `Ledger`) would be affected. Also, describe how the `projections_service` would need to be updated to reflect these auto-payments in its read models (e.g., for student dashboards).
5.  **Compliance and Consent:** Referencing the principles in `docs/architecture/05_security_and_compliance.md` and `docs/lessons/L03_Regulatory_Compliance_in_Code.md`, explain how your design handles the student's opt-in consent. Where would this consent flag be stored and how would it be checked in the workflow?
6.  **Affected Components:** List the key files and components (e.g., specific use cases, handlers, domain models, infrastructure) that would require modification to implement your design.

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would begin by thoroughly reviewing the existing architecture documentation, especially `02_microservices_and_bounded_contexts.md`, `03_cqrs_and_event_sourcing.md`, and `04_saga_pattern.md`. They would recognize that this is a classic distributed transaction problem perfectly suited for the existing Saga pattern.

The developer would inspect `financial_aid_service/application/use_cases/disburse_stipend_saga.c` to understand how stipends are currently processed. They would identify that the `StipendDisbursed` event, published via RabbitMQ (`rabbitmq_publisher.c`), is the logical trigger for the new functionality.

Their proposed design would likely extend the existing `DisburseStipendSaga` rather than creating a new one, arguing that applying funds to tuition is part of the overall stipend disbursement process. This keeps the transaction context unified.

The proposal would outline a new step in the saga that occurs after the stipend is successfully disbursed. This step would issue a command, like `ApplyStipendToTuition`, to the `bursar_service`. Before issuing the command, the saga coordinator would first need to query a read model to check for two conditions: (1) the student's opt-in status and (2) an outstanding balance. This query would target a projection maintained by the `projections_service` or a query endpoint on the `bursar_service`.

The design would define new events like `StipendAppliedToTuition` and `StipendApplicationToTuitionFailed`. It would also define a compensating action, `ReverseTuitionApplication`, for the saga in case a subsequent step fails.

Finally, the developer would trace the impact through the system: the `bursar_service` command handler would update the `Account` and `Ledger` aggregates, persisting the new events to the `postgres_event_store`. The `projections_service` would need a new event handler in a file like `dashboard_projector.c` to consume the `StipendAppliedToTuition` event and update the student's account balance projection.

## Evaluation Criteria

- **Pattern Adherence:** Correctly identifies and proposes extending the existing Saga pattern, respecting the CQRS/ES flow.
- **Component Identification:** Accurately identifies the roles of `financial_aid_service`, `bursar_service`, `projections_service`, and the Saga Coordinator.
- **Data Flow Correctness:** Proposes a logical and correct sequence of events, commands, and queries, including the crucial pre-condition check.
- **Event Design:** Defines specific and meaningful new domain events appropriate for the feature.
- **Compliance Integration:** Explicitly addresses the student consent requirement and correctly places the check in the workflow, referencing the compliance documentation.
- **Codebase Awareness:** Demonstrates understanding of the codebase by correctly identifying key files/modules that would need modification (e.g., `disburse_stipend_saga.c`, `dashboard_projector.c`).
- **Justification Quality:** Provides clear reasoning for architectural decisions, such as choosing to extend the existing saga versus creating a new one.

     2→# EduPay Ledger Academy  
     3→*A production-grade, clean-architecture fintech platform written in C.*
     4→
     5→---
     6→

     8→
     9→EduPay Ledger Academy is a **reference implementation** of enterprise-level payment rails tailored for higher-education.  
    10→Unlike toy examples, the codebase powers real tuition, stipend, and scholarship flows **while doubling as a living textbook** for computer-science curricula.
    11→
    12→* Clean Architecture (Robert C. Martin) – every policy is isolated from frameworks.  
    13→* Domain-Driven Design – bounded contexts for Admissions, Bursar, Financial-Aid, and Continuing-Education.  
    14→* Event Sourcing + CQRS – immutable audit trail and low-latency read models.  
    15→* Saga Orchestration – optional chaos-engineering labs for distributed rollbacks.  
    16→* PCI-DSS / FERPA / PSD2 compliance patterns baked-in.
    17→
    18→> “We don’t hide complexity from students—we instrument it.”  
    19→> — *Academic Advisory Board, 2024*

    11→
    12→# Micro-services & Bounded Contexts
    13→
    14→EduPay Ledger Academy follows Domain-Driven Design and splits the
    15→business domain into **four bounded contexts** (BCs).  Each BC is
    16→implemented as one or more micro-services—small autonomous executables
    17→written in C and packaged as OCI containers.
    18→
    19→| Bounded Context         | Canonical Service | Purpose                                                                    |
    20→|-------------------------|-------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------|
    21→| Admissions              | `admissions-api`  | On-boards students, allocates student-ids, emits *StudentRegistered*       |
    22→| Bursar (A/R)            | `ledger-core`     | Double-entry ledger, tuition invoicing, GL postings, payment gateway       |
    23→| Financial-Aid           | `aid-engine`      | Award rules, stipend disbursement, compliance (FERPA / PSD2 / PCI-DSS)     |
    24→| Continuing-Education    | `micro-cred`      | Per-course micro-credential tracking, pay-per-module split-payments         |
    25→
    26→A **Shared-Kernel** provides value-objects (`Money`, `Currency`,
    27→`StudentId`) and the **AuditTrail** event store.
    28→
    29→```

     3→title: EduPay Ledger Academy – CQRS & Event Sourcing Architecture
     4→description: Technical deep-dive into how the EduPay Ledger Academy executes Command-Query Responsibility Segregation (CQRS) and Event Sourcing in C while remaining faithful to Clean Architecture.
     5→slug: /architecture/cqrs-and-event-sourcing
     6→---
     7→
     8→# 03 – CQRS & Event Sourcing
     9→
    10→> “Separate **what** the system does from **what** the system knows.”  
    11→> — EduPay Core Team
    12→
    13→EduPay Ledger Academy employs **CQRS** to divide **mutations** (Commands) from **reads** (Queries) so that educators can swap persistence technologies, message buses, or reporting databases without touching domain logic.   
    14→All state-changing requests are persisted as **immutable domain events**, enabling deterministic replay, powerful audit trails, and student-friendly time-travel debugging.
    15→
    16→---
    17→
    18→## Table of Contents
    19→
    20→1. Domain Vocabulary  
    21→2. High Level Flow Diagram  
    22→3. Command Pipeline (Write Model)  
    23→4. Event Store Implementation (C)  
    24→5. Query Model & Projections  
    25→6. Consistency, Concurrency, and Idempotency  
    26→7. Failure Injection Labs  
    27→8. Further Reading
    28→
    29→---
    30→
    31→## 1. Domain Vocabulary
    32→
    33→Term | Definition
    34→---- | ----------
    35→**Command** | An intent _to do_ something. Must either succeed or return an error.
    36→**Event** | A fact _that something happened_. Can never change or be removed.
    37→**Aggregate** | A transactional consistency boundary, e.g., `LedgerAccount`.
    38→**Projection / Read Model** | A denormalized view optimized for reads: dashboards, ledgers, etc.
    39→

     1→```markdown
     2→# EduPay Ledger Academy  
     3→### docs/architecture/04_saga_pattern.md
     4→---
     5→> Version: 1.3  
     6→> Last Reviewed: 2024-05-09  
     7→> Authors: Core Platform Team (@edupay-ledger)  
     8→> Status: ✅ Production  
     9→---
    10→
    11→## 1. Why EduPay Uses the Saga Pattern
    12→
    13→EduPay processes **millions of distributed, financial micro-transactions** each semester.  
    14→The platform deliberately avoids *single-phase* database transactions because:
    15→
    16→* **Micro-services** compose payments from multiple bounded contexts (Admissions, Bursar, Treasury, FX, Fraud).  
    17→* **Heterogeneous data stores** (PostgreSQL, Redis, EventStoreDB) participate in a single business flow.  
    18→* **Resiliency labs** in coursework require controlled failure injection and roll-back.  
    19→
    20→A **Saga** slices a long-running business process into a series of *local* ACID transactions plus **compensating steps**.  
    21→If any step fails, the orchestrator triggers rollback actions in **reverse order**, yielding *eventual consistency* without locking global resources.
    22→
    23→```
    24→Enrollment_Fee → FX_Conversion → Treasury_Posting → Fraud_Scoring → Receipt_Email
    25→         │                │                │              │
    26→         └────────────────┴────────────────┴──────────────┴─────┐
    27→                       Saga Orchestrator (payment_saga.c)       │
    28→                       • persists state in Audit_Trail          │
    29→                       • broadcasts events over EventBus        │
    30→                       • drives rollbacks on failure ◄──────────┘
    31→```
    32→
    33→---
    34→
    35→## 2. High-Level Flow
    36→
    37→1. **Create** a `payment
... (truncated)

     7→ * This file defines the canonical Money value-object used across every
     8→ * bounded-context (Admissions, Bursar, Financial-Aid, etc.).  The structure is
     9→ * purposely framework-agnostic so that educators can swap persistence layers,
    10→ * message brokers, or UI shells without impacting business rules.
    11→ *
    12→ * Design notes
    13→ * ------------
    14→ * 1. Amount is stored in the *minor* unit (e.g., cents) as a 64-bit signed
    15→ *    integer to avoid floating-point rounding errors.
    16→ * 2. ISO-4217 alpha-3 currency codes are used.  Validation is built-in so
    17→ *    erroneous codes are rejected early.
    18→ * 3. All operations guarantee currency homogeneity; cross-currency math must
    19→ *    be handled by the FX service in the multi-currency bounded context.
    20→ * 4. Overflow checks leverage compiler intrinsics when available
    21→ *    (__builtin_add_overflow / __builtin_mul_overflow).  Fallback logic is
    22→ *    provided for non-GNU/Clang toolchains.
    23→ * 5. This header is fully self-contained: implementation is declared `static
    24→ *    inline` so that business-rule code can include it directly without
    25→ *    linking.
    26→ */

60-assistanttool_useRead
61-usertool_resultRead
     1→```markdown
     2→# EduPay Ledger Academy  
     3→### docs/architecture/04_saga_pattern.md
     4→---
     5→> Version: 1.3  
     6→> Last Reviewed: 2024-05-09  
     7→> Authors: Core Platform Team (@edupay-ledger)  
     8→> Status: ✅ Production  
     9→---
    10→
    11→## 1. Why EduPay Uses the Saga Pattern
    12→
    13→EduPay processes **millions of distributed, financial micro-transactions** each semester.  
    14→The platform deliberately avoids *single-phase* database transactions because:
    15→
    16→* **Micro-services** compose payments from multiple bounded contexts (Admissions, Bursar, Treasury, FX, Fraud).  
    17→* **Heterogeneous data stores** (PostgreSQL, Redis, EventStoreDB) participate in a single business flow.  
    18→* **Resiliency labs** in coursework require controlled failure injection and roll-back.  
    19→
    20→A **Saga** slices a long-running business process into a series of *local* ACID transactions plus **compensating steps**.  
    21→If any step fails, the orchestrator triggers rollback actions in **reverse order**, yielding *eventual consistency* without locking global resources.
    22→
    23→```
    24→Enrollment_Fee → FX_Conversion → Treasury_Posting → Fraud_Scoring → Receipt_Email
    25→         │                │                │              │
    26→         └────────────────┴────────────────┴──────────────┴─────┐
    27→                       Saga Orchestrator (payment_saga.c)       │
    28→                       • persists state in Audit_Trail          │
    29→                       • broadcasts events over EventBus        │
    30→                       • drives rollbacks on failure ◄──────────┘
    31→```
    32→
    33→---
    34→
    35→## 2. High-Level Flow
    36→
    37→1. **Create** a `payment
... (truncated)

     3→EduPay Ledger Academy (ELA) treats confidentiality, integrity, and availability as first-class
     4→requirements.  Because the platform is intended both for **production payment flows** and for
     5→**pedagogical deep-dives**, every security control is written in C with pristine readability,
     6→strong encapsulation, and complete unit-test coverage.
     7→
     8→This document serves three audiences:
     9→

    22→| Student PII (FERPA)            | Deanonymize academic records            | Record-level field encryption, Attribute-based access control (ABAC)                   |

    11→
    12→# Micro-services & Bounded Contexts
    13→
    14→EduPay Ledger Academy follows Domain-Driven Design and splits the
    15→business domain into **four bounded contexts** (BCs).  Each BC is
    16→implemented as one or more micro-services—small autonomous executables
    17→written in C and packaged as OCI containers.
    18→
    19→| Bounded Context         | Canonical Service | Purpose                                                                    |
    20→|-------------------------|-------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------|
    21→| Admissions              | `admissions-api`  | On-boards students, allocates student-ids, emits *StudentRegistered*       |
    22→| Bursar (A/R)            | `ledger-core`     | Double-entry ledger, tuition invoicing, GL postings, payment gateway       |
    23→| Financial-Aid           | `aid-engine`      | Award rules, stipend disbursement, compliance (FERPA / PSD2 / PCI-DSS)     |
    24→| Continuing-Education    | `micro-cred`      | Per-course micro-credential tracking, pay-per-module split-payments         |
    25→
    26→A **Shared-Kernel** provides value-objects (`Money`, `Currency`,
    27→`StudentId`) and the **AuditTrail** event store.
    28→
    29→```

     1→```markdown
     2→---
     3→title: EduPay Ledger Academy – CQRS & Event Sourcing Architecture
     4→description: Technical deep-dive into how the EduPay Ledger Academy executes Command-Query Responsibility Segregation (CQRS) and Event Sourcing in C while remaining faithful to Clean Architecture.
     5→slug: /architecture/cqrs-and-event-sourcing
     6→---
     7→
     8→# 03 – CQRS & Event Sourcing
     9→
    10→> “Separate **what** the system does from **what** the system knows.”  
    11→> — EduPay Core Team
    12→
    13→EduPay Ledger Academy employs **CQRS** to divide **mutations** (Commands) from **reads** (Queries) so that educators can swap persistence technologies, message buses, or reporting databases without touching domain logic.   
    14→All state-changing requests are persisted as **immutable domain events**, enabling deterministic replay, powerful audit trails, and student-friendly time-travel debugging.
    15→
    16→---
    17→
    18→## Table of Contents
    19→
    20→1. Domain Vocabulary  
    21→2. High Level Flow Diagram  
    22→3. Command Pipeline (Write Model)  
    23→4. Event Store Implementation (C)  
    24→5. Query Model & Projections  
    25→6. Consistency, Concurrency, and Idempotency  
    26→7. Failure Injection Labs  
    27→8. Further Reading
    28→
    29→---
    30→
    31→## 1. Domain Vocabulary
    32→
    33→Term | Definition
    34→---- | ----------
    35→**Command** | An intent _to do_ something. Must either succeed or return an error.
    36→**Event** | A fact _that something happened_. Can never change or be removed.
    37→**Aggregate** | A transactional consistency boundary, e.g., `LedgerAccount`.
    38→**Projection / Read Model** | A denormalized view optimized for reads: dashboards, ledgers, etc.
    39→
... (truncated)

     4→ * @brief  Domain Model:  Bursar ‑ Ledger Account Aggregate
     5→ *
     6→ * The Account aggregate is the canonical representation of a student’s financial
     7→ * ledger inside the Bursar bounded-context.  It is intentionally persistence-agnostic
     8→ * (Clean Architecture) and contains only business rules.  Orchestration with
     9→ * payments gateways, SQL/NoSQL stores, or message brokers is delegated to the
    10→ * outer “infrastructure” layer.
    11→ *
    12→ * Thread-Safety:
    13→ *  – All mutating functions receive a pointer to the aggregate instance and MUST
    14→ *    be protected by the calling application’s concurrency strategy
    15→ *    (mutex, actor model, etc.).  The domain layer purposefully remains
    16→ *    synchronization-free to avoid bleeding implementation details inward.
    17→ *
    18→ * Monetary Representation:
    19→ *  – Amounts are stored as signed 64-bit integers representing the smallest
    20→ *    denomination (“minor units”, e.g. cents) to avoid floating-point error.

     1→/**
     2→ * @file ledger.h
     3→ * @author
     4→ *   EduPay Ledger Academy — Bursar Service
     5→ *
     6→ * @brief Domain-level abstractions for the immutable double-entry ledger
     7→ *        maintained by the Bursar bounded-context.
     8→ *
     9→ * The Ledger component is *framework-agnostic* and contains **no** references
    10→ * to databases, loggers, message brokers or HTTP frameworks.  This guarantees
    11→ * that students can swap infrastructure while the core business rules remain
    12→ * stable—a key property of Robert C. Martin’s Clean Architecture.
    13→ *
    14→ * All monetary calculations use fixed-precision integers (minor units) to avoid
    15→ * floating-point rounding errors.  ISO-4217 alpha-3 currency codes are used
    16→ * for multi-currency support.
    17→ *
    18→ * Conventions
    19→ * -----------
    20→ * • All functions return 0 on success, non-zero `ledger_err_t` codes on failure.  
    21→ * • “Immutable” means _append-only_; once an entry is POSTED it can only be
    22→ *   compensated by a REVERSAL entry—never mutated in place.  
    23→ * • Thread-safety: read-only operations are lock-free; mutating operations
    24→ *   require the caller to provide a concurrency control strategy (e.g. external
    25→ *   mutex, optimistic CAS or sequential command bus).
    26→ */
    27→

I have created a comprehensive architectural proposal document at `/logs/agent/solution.md`. Let me provide a summary of the key points:

## Summary of Architectural Proposal

The document outlines a complete design for the **Tuition Auto-Payment** feature with the following key decisions:

### 1. Saga Pattern Integration
- **Extends the existing `DisburseStipendSaga`** (at `/app/project/src/services/financial_aid_service/application/use_cases/disburse_stipend_saga.h`) rather than creating a new saga
- Adds a new Step 6 that occurs after stipend disbursement but before saga completion
- Includes compensation logic (`reverse_tuition_application`) for rollback scenarios

### 2. Interaction Flow
- Step 7a: Query the projections service for student's opt-in status and outstanding balance
- Step 7b: If opt-in=true AND balance>0, send `ApplyStipendToTuition` command to bursar_service
- The bursar service debits student's stipend funds and credits the tuition receivable account

### 3. New Domain Events
- `StipendAppliedToTuition` - Published by bursar_service on success
- `StipendApplicationToTuitionFailed` - Published when application fails
- `TuitionApplicationReversed` - Published during saga compensation

### 4. CQRS/Event Sourcing Impact
- **Account aggregate** and **Ledger aggregate** in bursar_service process the auto-payment
- **Dashboard projector** needs new event handlers for the new event types
- New SQLite tables for consent tracking and payment history

### 5. Compliance and Consent
- Consent stored in `student_auto_payment_preferences` table owned by admissions_service
- Default is `opt_in_consent = false` (FERPA compliant)
- Consent check happens at execution time in Step 7a
- All consent changes are event-sourced for audit

### 6. Key Affected Files
- `disbur

ENOHANDLER, EHANDLER\n\n**Command Definition (DTOs):**\n```c\ntypedef struct edu_command {\n    const char *name;         // Command key\n    const void *payload;      // Immutable payload\n    size_t      payload_sz;   // Payload size\n} edu_command_t;\n```\n\n**Query Bus:** `/app/project/src/core/cqrs/query_bus.h`\n- Similar architecture for read-side queries\n- Separate from command path for scalability\n\n### 3.2 EVENT SOURCING\n\n**File:** `/app/project/src/core/event_sourcing/event_store_interface.h` (287 lines)\n\n**Core Concepts:**\n- **Immutable append-only event log** \u2013 all state changes recorded as events\n- **Aggregate versioning** \u2013 optimistic concurrency control via version numbers\n- **Snapshots** \u2013 periodic state snapshots to accelerate rehydration\n- **Live subscriptions** \u2013 at-least-once delivery to subscribers\n\n**Event Store Interface (V-Table Pattern):**\n```c\ntypedef struct {\n    event_store_result_t (*append_to_stream)(\n        event_store_t *store,\n        const char *stream_name,\n        const event_store_record_t *events,\n        size_t event_count,\n        uint64_t expected_version);\n    \n    event_store_result_t (*read_stream)(...);\n    event_store_result_t (*read_all)(...);\n    event_store_result_t (*set_snapshot)(...);\n    event_store_result_t (*subscribe)(...);\n    // ... more operations\n} event_store_ops_t;\n```\n\n**Event Record Structure:**\n```c\ntypedef struct {\n    event_store_uuid_t event_id;\n    char aggregate_type[64];        // \"StudentAccount\", \"Ledger\", etc.\n    event_store_uuid_t aggregate_id;\n    uint64_t aggregate_version;     // Optimistic concurrency token\n    char event_type[64];            // \"StudentEnrolled\", \"PaymentAuthorized\", etc.\n    uint8_t *payload;               // JSON/MessagePack/Protobuf (opaque)\n    size_t payload_size;\n    time_t timestamp_utc;\n} event_store_record_t;\n```\n\n**Event Definition:** `/app/project/src/core/event_sourcing/event.h` (338 lines)\n- UUID v4 generation (RFC-4122 compliant)\n- Binary serialization with magic number (0xEDUPA7A)\n- Format: `[magic(4)][meta][payloadLen(4)][payload]`\n- Max payload: 4096 bytes (safety bound)\n\n**Idempotent Processing:**\n- Projection metadata tracks `last_sequence` to detect replayed events\n- At-least-once delivery from event bus guarantees no loss\n\n### 3.3 SAGA PATTERN IMPLEMENTATION\n\n**File:** `/app/project/src/core/saga/saga_definition.h` (296 lines)\n\n**Saga Concept:**\nDistributed transaction across multiple services using compensating transactions (compensations triggered in reverse order on failure).\n\n**Saga Definition Structure:**\n```c\ntypedef struct saga_step {\n    uint8_t               id;\n    const char           *name;\n    saga_step_action_fn   forward_action;      // Primary business logic\n    saga_step_action_fn   compensation_action; // Rollback logic\n    saga_step_state_t     state;\n} saga_step_t;\n\ntypedef struct saga_definition {\n    const char    *saga_name;           // e.g., \"TuitionPayment\"\n    struct { uint16_t major, minor, patch; } version;\n    saga_step_t   steps[SAGA_MAX_STEPS];\n    uint8_t       step_count;\n} saga_definition_t;\n```\n\n**Saga Coordinator:** `/app/project/src/core/saga/saga_coordinator.h`\n- Orchestrates step execution\n- Manages state transitions\n- Triggers compensation chain on failure\n\n**Stipend Disbursement Saga Example:**\n\n**File:** `/app/project/src/services/financial_aid_service/application/use_cases/disburse_stipend_saga.h`\n\n**Step Sequence:**\n1. **Validate eligibility** (no compensation needed)\n2. **Reserve budget** \u2192 store `reservation_id`\n   - Fail point 1: release budget\n3. **Initiate transfer** (payment network) \u2192 store `network_tx_id`\n   - Fail point 2: release budget, reverse transfer\n4. **Record ledger entry**\n   - Fail point 3: reverse transfer, release budget, record reversal\n5. **Publish domain event**\n   - Fail point 4: all compensations (record reversal, reverse transfer, release budget)\n\n**Compensation Characteristics:**\n- **Idempotent** \u2013 safe to run multiple times\n- **Reverse order** \u2013 step 4 compensation runs before step 3's, etc.\n- **Error propagation** \u2013 maintains error context through chain\n\n**VTable Injection Pattern:**\n```c\ntypedef bool (*validate_eligibility_fn)(...);\ntypedef bool (*reserve_budget_fn)(...);\ntypedef bool (*release_budget_fn)(...);\ntypedef bool (*initiate_transfer_fn)(...);\ntypedef bool (*reverse_transfer_fn)(...);\ntypedef bool (*record_ledger_entry_fn)(...);\ntypedef bool (*publish_domain_event_fn)(...);\n\ntypedef struct {\n    validate_eligibility_fn validate_eligibility;\n    reserve_budget_fn reserve_budget;\n    release_budget_fn release_budget;\n    initiate_transfer_fn initiate_transfer;\n    reverse_transfer_fn reverse_transfer;\n    record_ledger_entry_fn record_ledger_entry;\n    publish_domain_event_fn publish_domain_event;\n} stipend_disbursement_callbacks_t;\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. SHARED KERNEL \u2013 VALUE OBJECTS & UTILITIES\n\n**Path:** `/app/project/src/shared_kernel/`\n\n### 4.1 Domain Value Objects\n\n**Money (Value Object):** `/app/project/src/shared_kernel/domain/money.h` (330 lines)\n\n**Purpose:** Cross-context canonical representation of monetary amounts\n\n**Features:**\n- **Immutable by convention** \u2013 all operations return new instances\n- **Minor units storage** \u2013 amounts in cents/pence to avoid floating-point errors\n- **ISO-4217 currency codes** \u2013 3-letter codes (USD, EUR, JPY, etc.)\n- **Overflow detection** \u2013 uses `__builtin_add_overflow` / `__builtin_mul_overflow` (GCC/Clang) with fallback\n- **Header-only** \u2013 no external dependencies (C standard library only)\n\n**API:**\n```c\nMoneyError money_create(Money *out, const char *currency, int64_t amount_minor);\nMoneyError money_add(const Money *a, const Money *b, Money *out);\nMoneyError money_subtract(const Money *a, const Money *b, Money *out);\nMoneyError money_multiply(const Money *a, int64_t factor, Money *out);\nint money_compare(const Money *a, const Money *b);\nMoneyError money_allocate(const Money *total, size_t n, Money *out_parts);\n```\n\n**Example: Allocating bursary across N recipients**\n```c\nMoney total = { .amount_minor = 100000, .currency = \"USD\" };\nMoney parts[5];\nmoney_allocate(&total, 5, parts);  // Distributes with remainder handling\n```\n\n**Other Value Objects:**\n- `/app/project/src/shared_kernel/domain/student_id.h` \u2013 Canonical student identifier\n- `/app/project/src/shared_kernel/domain/transaction_id.h` \u2013 Transaction reference\n\n### 4.2 Infrastructure Utilities\n\n**Cryptography:** `/app/project/src/shared_kernel/infrastructure/crypto/`\n- `aescrypto.h` \u2013 AES-256-GCM for PII encryption (FERPA compliance)\n- `hash.h` \u2013 Secure hashing\n\n**Logging:** `/app/project/src/shared_kernel/infrastructure/logger.h`\n- Structured logging with log levels\n- Thread-safe output\n\n---\n\n## 5. KEY ARCHITECTURAL PATTERNS\n\n### 5.1 Clean Architecture Layering\n\n**Dependency Rule:** Outer layers know inner layers, never vice-versa.\n\n**Layers (from innermost to outermost):**\n\n1. **Domain Layer** (most stable, no I/O)\n   - Value objects (Money, StudentId)\n   - Business rules (payment logic, eligibility checks)\n   - **Example:** `/app/project/src/services/bursar_service/domain/`\n\n2. **Application Layer** (use cases)\n   - Orchestrates domain objects\n   - Translates DTOs to domain objects\n   - **Example:** `/app/project/src/services/bursar_service/application/use_cases/process_tuition_payment.h`\n   - Use case entry point with injected ports (fraud check, payment gateway, ledger)\n\n3. **Interface Layer** (replaceable)\n   - HTTP controllers, gRPC adapters, CLI handlers\n   - **Example:** `/app/project/src/services/bursar_service/interfaces/controllers/http_payment_controller.h`\n   - JSON presenters for API responses\n\n4. **Infrastructure Layer** (volatile, frameworks)\n   - PostgreSQL event store, RabbitMQ publishers, payment gateways\n   - **Example:** `/app/project/src/services/bursar_service/infrastructure/persistence/postgres_event_store.h`\n\n### 5.2 Dependency Inversion via Function Pointers\n\n**Pattern:** All I/O dependencies expressed as `struct` containing function pointers (V-tables).\n\n**Example from bursar service:**\n```c\ntypedef struct {\n    port_fraud_check_t       fraud_check;\n    port_reserve_funds_t     reserve_funds;\n    port_post_ledger_entry_t post_ledger;\n    port_write_audit_trail_t write_audit;\n} process_tuition_payment_interactor_t;\n\n// Called as:\nstatic inline edu_tuition_status_t process_tuition_payment(\n    const process_tuition_payment_interactor_t *interactor,\n    const process_tuition_payment_request_t *request,\n    process_tuition_payment_response_t *response) {\n    // ... business logic ...\n    if (!interactor->fraud_check(request, fraud_reason)) { ... }\n    if (!interactor->reserve_funds(request, txn_id, gateway_error)) { ... }\n}\n```\n\n**Benefits:**\n- **Testability** \u2013 inject mocks without recompilation\n- **Swappability** \u2013 replace PostgreSQL with SQLite for labs\n- **Framework independence** \u2013 core domain touches zero frameworks\n\n### 5.3 Message Bus & Event Publishing\n\n**Broker Stub (Pedagogical):** `/app/project/src/services/bursar_service/main.c` lines 177-224\n\nFor teaching purposes, the broker is modeled as STDIN/STDOUT:\n- Events received on STDIN (line-delimited format)\n- Events published to STDOUT\n- Professors swap in real AMQP/Kafka without touching business logic\n\n**Example Protocol:**\n```\nInput:  TUITION_DUE student_id=S123 amount=12500 currency=USD\nOutput: LEDGER_UPDATED student_id=S123 balance=12500 currency=USD\n```\n\n### 5.4 Idempotency & At-Least-Once Delivery\n\n**Pattern:** Event projectors track processed sequences\n\n**Dashboard Projector Implementation:**\n```c\n// In projection_metadata table:\nCREATE TABLE projection_metadata (\n    id           INTEGER PRIMARY KEY,\n    last_sequence INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0\n);\n\n// On event arrival:\nif (evt->sequence <= last_seq) return; // Already processed\n// ... apply fold ...\n_update_last_sequence(db, evt->sequence);\n```\n\n**Guarantees:**\n- If an event is delivered twice, it's folded only once\n- On projector restart, replay from last known position\n- Prevents double-counting in read models\n\n---\n\n## 6.                   \u2502 Response: TUITION_OK, txn_id\n                   \u2193\n Bus     \u2502\n    \u2502 event: PaymentAuthorized \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n             \u2502\n \u2502\n             \u2193                    \u2193\n    \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510 (immutable)  \u2502     \u2502 Model (SQLite)   \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518     \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n**Key Observations:**\n1. **Fraud check first** \u2013 reject early before gateway calls\n2. **Gateway interaction outside ledger** \u2013 network failures don't affect core transaction\n3. **Ledger entry post-authorization** \u2013 only committed amounts recorded\n4. **Audit trail separate** \u2013 audit failures don't roll back payments\n5. **Event published** \u2013 async projections update read models\n\n---\n\n## 7. KEY COMPONENT SUMMARY TABLE\n\n| Component | Location | Lines | Purpose |\n|-----------|----------|-------|---------|\n| **Command Bus** | `src/core/cqrs/command_bus.h` | 330 | Thread-safe command dispatch w/ dynamic registration |\n| **Event Store Interface** | `src/core/event_sourcing/event_store_interface.h` | 287 | Pluggable event persistence (Postgres, DynamoDB, etc.) |\n| **Event Definition** | `src/core/event_sourcing/event.h` | 338 | UUID v4 generation, serialization, binary format |\n| **Saga Definition** | `src/core/saga/saga_definition.h` | 296 | Step composition, state machine, compensation tracking |\n| **Money Value Object** | `src/shared_kernel/domain/money.h` | 330 | Immutable monetary amounts, overflow detection |\n| **Bursar Main** | `src/services/bursar_service/main.c` | 502 | Service entry point, event loop, configuration |\n| **Process Tuition UC** | `src/services/bursar_service/application/use_cases/process_tuition_payment.h` | 339 | Payment orchestration with dependency injection |\n| **Stipend Saga** | `src/services/financial_aid_service/application/use_cases/disburse_stipend_saga.h` | 362 | 5-step saga with compensation chain |\n| **Dashboard Projector** | `src/projections_service/event_handlers/dashboard_projector.h` | 430 | SQLite read model folding, idempotent replay |\n\n---\n\n## 9. ARCHITECTURAL HIGHLIGHTS\n\n### 9.1 Why C?\n- **Direct control** \u2013 memory management teaches resource discipline\n- **No magic** \u2013 students see exact I/O, concurrency, serialization\n- **Educational** \u2013 runtime semantics visible (no JIT, GC, reflection surprises)\n- **Deployment** \u2013 tiny binaries, low latency (suitable for fintech)\n\n### 9.2 Framework Independence\n- **Zero external dependencies in domain** \u2013 only C17 standard library\n- **Adapters at periphery** \u2013 PostgreSQL, RabbitMQ, HTTP swapped without touching rules\n- **Testing friendly** \u2013 mock ports without framework setup\n\n### 9.3 Compliance Baked In\n- **PCI-DSS** \u2013 tokenization gateway, PAN never in core process memory\n- **FERPA** \u2013 AES-256-GCM encryption for PII, key rotation via Vault\n- **PSD2** \u2013 SCA patterns, WebAuthn support for continuing-education\n\n### 9.4 Saga Demo Mode\n**Feature:** `/app/project/src/services/bursar_service/main.c` line 456\n\nEnable with: `export EDUPAY_SAGA_MODE=1`\n\nSimulates failures every N events, forcing compensation chain execution. Professors use this to teach rollback scenarios in live labs.\n\n---\n\n## 10. HOW SERVICES COMMUNICATE\n\n### Event-Driven (Asynchronous)\n\n**Flow:**\n1. **Bursar publishes** `PaymentAuthorized` to message bus (NATS/Kafka/AMQP)\n2. **Financial Aid** subscribed to this event, triggers `disburse_stipend_saga`\n3. **Projections Service** subscribes to all events, folds into SQLite dashboard\n\n### Command-Query Separation\n\n**Write Path:**\n- HTTP POST /tuition/pay \u2192 Command Bus \u2192 Use Case \u2192 Domain Logic \u2192 Event Store\n\n**Read Path:**\n- HTTP GET /dashboard \u2192 Query Bus \u2192 Read Model (SQLite) \u2192 JSON Presenter\n\n**Benefits:**\n- Different persistence for writes (event log) vs. reads (denormalized index)\n- Projections lag writes but scale reads independently\n- Eventually consistent dashboards acceptable for reporting\n\n---\n\n## 11. DEPLOYMENT & EXTENSIBILITY\n\n### Swappable Infrastructure Examples\n\n**1. Replace Event Store:**\n```c\n// Today: PostgreSQL\nstruct event_store *store = postgres_event_store_create(...);\n\n// Tomorrow: SQLite (for lab exercises)\nstruct event_store *store = sqlite_event_store_create(...);\n\n// Code using store unchanged:\nevent_store_append(store, stream, events, count, version);\n```\n\n**2. Replace Message Broker:**\n```c\n// Today: STDIN/STDOUT (pedagogical)\nvoid broker_publish(const Message *msg) { fprintf(stdout, ...); }\n\n// Tomorrow: RabbitMQ\nvoid broker_publish(const Message *msg) { amqp_basic_publish(...); }\n\n// Bursar service unchanged:\nif (!process_message(&msg)) break;\n```\n\n**3. Replace Crypto:**\n- Default: AES-256-GCM (OpenSSL)\n- Lab: XOR cipher (insecure, for teaching only)\n- Production: Hardware security module (HSM) via PKCS#11\n\n---\n\n## 12. TESTING STRATEGY\n\n### Unit Tests (Domain Logic)\n- No I/O dependencies\n- Pure C functions\n- Mock ports injected\n\n### Integration Tests\n- Services in-process\n- Fake message broker (memory buffer)\n- SQLite instead of PostgreSQL\n\n### End-to-End Tests\n- Docker Compose (full stack)\n- Real PostgreSQL + RabbitMQ\n- Chaos injection (kill services mid-saga)\n\n---\n\n## FILE PATH REFERENCE FOR KEY COMPONENTS\n\n### Core Architecture (Read-Only, Framework-Agnostic)\n- `/app/project/src/core/cqrs/command_bus.h` \u2013 Command dispatch\n- Saga Pattern Demonstration Mode\n   109\u2192\n   110\u2192| Failure Point | Compensating Action | Teaching Objective |\n   111\u2192|---------------|--------------------|--------------------|\n   112\u2192| FX conversion timeout | Revert ledger entry | Idempotent rollbacks |\n   113\u2192| Scholarship ledger update fails | Re-credit student card | Distributed tracing |\n   114\u2192\n 121\u2192---\n   122\u2192\n   123\u2192## 7  Event Sourcing & CQRS\n   124\u2192\n   125\u2192* **Write Model** \u2013 append-only events stored in `audit/ledger.dat`\n   126\u2192* **Read Model** \u2013 projections in **PostgreSQL** (can swap with **SQLite** for\n   127\u2192  classroom labs)\n   128\u2192* Replay tool: `bin/ledger-replay --from 2022-01-01`\n   129\u2192\n   130\u2192---\n   131\u2192\n   132\u2192## 8  Security by Design\n   133\u2192\n   134\u21921. Memory-safe wrappers (`secure_mem.c`) protect against buffer overflows.\n   135\u21922. PCI-DSS scope is minimized by tokenizing PANs via external vault.\n   136\u21923. FERPA compliance: PII fields encrypted with **AES-256-GCM**; keys rotated\n   137\u2192   through **HashiCorp Vault** every 24 h.\n   138\u21924. Static analysis integrated with **clang-tidy** and **CodeQL**.\n   139\u2192\n   140\u2192---\n   141\u2192\n   142\u2192## 9  Extensibility: Swapping a Repository\n   143\u2192\n   144\u2192Example: Replace PostgreSQL with MongoDB in a lab.\n   145\u2192\n   146\u21921. Register the concrete type in `infra/repo_factory.c`.\n   151\u21923. No changes required in `usecase/process_payment.c`  \n   152\u2192   thanks to the **Dependency Inversion** rule.\n   153\u2192\n   154\u2192---\n   155\u2192\n   156\u2192## 10  Development Conventions\n   157\u2192\n   158\u2192* **C17** standard, compiled with `-Wall -Wextra -pedantic`.\n   159\u2192* One public header per component; internal helpers stay in `*.c`.\n   160\u2192* Unit tests with **Unity**; acceptance tests scripted in **Bats**.\n   161\u2192* Commit messages follow Conventional Commits:\n   162\u2192  `feat(bursar): add multi-currency rounding bugfix`.\n   163\u2192\n   164\u2192---\n   165\u2192\n   166\u2192## 11  Directory Tree (excerpt)\n   167\u2192\n   168\u2192```plaintext\n   169\u2192src/\n   170\u2192 \u251c\u2500 admissions/\n   171\u2192 \u2502   \u251c\u2500 domain/\n   172\u2192 \u2502   \u251c\u2500 usecase/\n   173\u2192 \u2502   \u2514\u2500 interface/\n   174\u2192 \u251c\u2500 bursar/\n   175\u2192 \u2502   \u2514\u2500 ...\n   176\u2192 \u251c\u2500 common/\n   177\u2192 \u2502   \u251c\u2500 secure_mem.c\n   178\u2192 \u2502   \u251c\u2500 currency.c\n   179\u2192 \u2502   \u2514\u2500 ...\n   180\u2192docs/\n   181\u2192 \u2514\u2500 architecture/\n   182\u2192     \u2514\u2500 README.md  \u2190 you are here\n   183\u2192tests/\n   184\u2192 \u251c\u2500 unit/\n   185\u2192 \u2514\u2500 integration/\n   186\u2192```\n   187\u2192\n   188\u2192---\n   189\u2192\n   190\u2192## 12  Future Work\n   191\u2192\n   192\u2192* Integrate OpenTelemetry for distributed tracing labs.\n   193\u2192* Add Rust FFI bindings to compare memory safety.\n   194\u2192* Implement ISO-20022 `pain.001` export for cross-border wires.\n   195\u2192\n   196\u2192---\n   197\u2192\n   198\u2192\u00a9 2023 EduPay Ledger Academy.  \n   199\u2192Licensed under the MIT License \u2013 see `LICENSE` for details.\n   200\u2192```\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. *invoice_id,\n   159\u2192                       const ep_money_t  *amount,\n   160\u2192                       const char        *auth_code)\n   161\u2192{\n   162\u2192    if (!repo || !bus || !invoice_id || !amount || !auth_code)\n   163\u2192        return -1; /* pre-condition failed */\n   164\u2192\n   165\u2192    if (repo->begin_tx(repo) != 0)\n   166\u2192        return  1; /* infra error */\n   167\u2192\n   168\u2192    if (repo->insert_ledger_entry(repo, invoice_id, amount, auth_code) != 0) {\n   169\u2192        repo->rollback_tx(repo);\n   170\u2192        return  2;\n   171\u2192    }\n   172\u2192\n   173\u2192    ep_payment_auth_t evt = {\n   174\u2192        .version        = PAYMENT_AUTH_VERSION,\n   175\u2192        .occurred_at_utc= time(NULL),\n   176\u2192    };\n   177\u2192    /* (Safe) string copy utilities omitted for brevity */\n   178\u2192    strncpy(evt.id,        \"UUID-GEN-STUB\", sizeof evt.id);\n   179\u2192    strncpy(evt.student_id,\"SID-LOOKUP-X\", sizeof evt.student_id);\n   180\u2192    strncpy(evt.invoice_id,invoice_id,     sizeof evt.invoice_id);\n   181\u2192    strncpy(evt.currency,  amount->currency, sizeof evt.currency);\n   182\u2192    evt.amount_minor = amount->amount_minor;\n   183\u2192    strncpy(evt.auth_code, auth_code, sizeof evt.auth_code);\n   184\u2192\n   185\u2192    if (bus->publish(bus, &evt, sizeof evt) != 0) {\n   186\u2192        repo->rollback_tx(repo);\n   187\u2192        return  3;\n   188\u2192    }\n   189\u2192\n   190\u2192    return repo->commit_tx(repo);\n   191\u2192}\n   192\u2192```\n   193\u2192\n   194\u2192### Saga Orchestrator (Distributed Tuition Payment)\n   195\u2192\n   196\u2192```c\n   197\u2192/* saga/tuition_payment_saga.h */\n   198\u2192#ifndef EP_SAGA_TUITION_PAYMENT_H\n   199\u2192#define EP_SAGA_TUITION_PAYMENT_H\n   200\u2192\n   201\u2192/*\n   202\u2192  TuitionPaymentSaga orchestrates:\n   203\u2192\n   204\u2192  1. Reserve Financial-Aid budget\n   205\u2192  2. Authorize card payment (Bursar)\n   206\u2192  3. Disburse stipends\n   207\u2192  4. Issue micro-credential revenue split\n   208\u2192\n   209\u2192  Compensation order is reverse.\n   210\u2192\n   211\u2192  State machine is stored in the EventStore; students step through\n   212\u2192  failures during outage simulations.\n   213\u2192*/\n   214\u2192\n   215\u2192typedef enum {\n   216\u2192    SAGA_STEP_NONE = 0,\n   217\u2192    SAGA_STEP_AID_RESERVED,\n   218\u2192    SAGA_STEP_PAYMENT_AUTHORIZED,\n   219\u2192    SAGA_STEP_STIPEND_PAID,\n   220\u2192    SAGA_STEP_MICROCRED_SPLIT,\n   221\u2192    SAGA_STEP_DONE,\n   222\u2192    SAGA_STEP_FAILED\n   223\u2192} ep_saga_state_t;\n   224\u2192\n   225\u2192#endif /* EP_SAGA_TUITION_PAYMENT_H */\n   226\u2192```\n   227\u2192\n   228\u2192## Anti-corruption Layer (ACL) Sample\n   229\u2192\n   230\u2192Admissions uses an external vendor for SIS and must translate its JSON\n   231\u2192schema into *StudentRegistered* events.\n   232\u2192\n   233\u2192```c\n   234\u2192/* acl/sis_adapter.c */\n   235\u2192#include <jansson.h>\n   236\u2192#include \"events/student_registered.h\"\n   237\u2192\n   238\u2192/* Returns 0 on success */\n   239\u2192int ep_acl_translate_sis_event(const char *json,\n   240\u2192                               ep_student_reg_t *out_evt)\n   241\u2192{\n   242\u2192    json_error_t err;\n   243\u2192    json_t *root = json_loads(json, 0, &err);\n   244\u2192    if (!root) return -1;\n   245\u2192\n   246\u2192    const char *sid   = json_string_value(json_object_get(root, \"sid\"));\n   247\u2192    const char *email = json_string_value(json_object_get(root, \"email\"));\n   248\u2192    if (!sid || !email) {\n   249\u2192        json_decref(root);\n   250\u2192        return -2;\n   251\u2192    }\n   252\u2192\n   253\u2192    strncpy(out_evt->student_id, sid, sizeof out_evt->student_id);\n   254\u2192    strncpy(out_evt->email,      email, sizeof out_evt->email);\n   255\u2192    out_evt->occurred_at_utc = time(NULL);\n   256\u2192\n   257\u2192    json_decref(root);\n   258\u2192    return 0;\n   259\u2192}\n   260\u2192```\n   261\u2192\n   262\u2192## Data Ownership & ACID Boundaries\n   263\u2192\n   264\u2192* **Admissions** owns `Student` aggregate; others reference via SID.\n   265\u2192* **Ledger-core** owns `Invoice`, `LedgerEntry`.\n   266\u2192* **Financial-Aid** owns `Award`, `AidDisbursement`.\n   267\u2192* Shared Kernel\u2019s `AuditTrail` is append-only; no service can mutate.\n   268\u2192\n   269\u2192| Service        | DB Schema          | Tx Boundary (Local ACID)    |\n   270\u2192|----------------|--------------------|-----------------------------|\n   271\u2192| admissions     | `admissions.*`     | `Student`, `Applicant`      |\n   272\u2192| ledger-core    | `ledger.*`         | `Invoice`, `LedgerEntry`    |\n   273\u2192| aid-engine     | `aid.*`            | `Award`, `Disbursement`     |\n   274\u2192| micro-cred     | `microcred.*`      | `CourseRun`, `SplitPayout`  |\n   275\u2192\n   276\u2192## Resilience Policy\n   277\u2192\n   278\u21921. Idempotent command handlers.\n   279\u21922. At-least-once event delivery (NATS JetStream).\n   280\u21923. Circuit-breaker around external PSP, open after 3 failures / 30 s.\n   281\u21924. Saga compensation for inter-context failure.\n   282\u2192\n   283\u2192```c\n   284\u2192/* infra/circuit_breaker.h */\n   285\u2192#ifndef EP_INFRA_CIRCUIT_BREAKER_H\n   286\u2192#define EP_INFRA_CIRCUIT_BREAKER_H\n   287\u2192#include <time.h>\n   288\u2192typedef enum { CB_CLOSED, CB_OPEN, CB_HALF_OPEN } cb_state_t;\n   289\u2192\n   290\u2192typedef struct circuit_breaker {\n   291\u2192    cb_state_t state;\n   292\u2192    unsigned   failure_count;\n   293\u2192    time_t     last_failure;\n   294\u2192    unsigned   open_timeout_sec;\n   295\u2192    unsigned   threshold;\n   296\u2192} circuit_breaker_t;\n   297\u2192\n   298\u2192void cb_init(circuit_breaker_t *cb,\n   299\u2192             unsigned threshold,\n   300\u2192             unsigned open_timeout_sec);\n   301\u2192\n   302\u2192int  cb_before_request(circuit_breaker_t *cb);\n   303\u2192void cb_after_success(circuit_breaker_t *cb);\n   304\u2192void cb_after_failure(circuit_breaker_t *cb);\n   305\u2192\n   306\u2192#endif /* EP_INFRA_CIRCUIT_BREAKER_H */\n   307\u2192```\n   308\u2192\n   309\u2192## Build & Deployment Standards\n   310\u2192\n   311\u2192* `Dockerfile` uses scratch + `musl-clang` static linking \u21d2 6 MB images.\n   312\u2192* Each service exports `/livez` and `/readyz` over HTTP on port 8080.\n   313\u2192* Kubernetes Helm charts pin CPU/memory, configure HPA on NATS lag.\n   314\u2192\n   315\u2192---\n   316\u2192\n   317\u2192> \u201cArchitecture is about the important stuff\u2014whatever that is.\u201d  \n   318\u2192> \u2014 Ralph Johnson\n   319\u2192\n   320\u2192Learners should fork this repository, enable **Saga Pattern\n   321\u2192Demonstration Mode** (`make chaos-on`), and trigger the `tuition\n   322\u2192checkout` flow. "     1\u2192```markdown\n     2\u2192---\n     3\u2192title: EduPay Ledger Academy \u2013 CQRS & Event Sourcing Architecture\n     4\u2192description: Technical deep-dive into how the EduPay Ledger Academy executes Command-Query Responsibility Segregation (CQRS) and Event Sourcing in C while remaining faithful to Clean Architecture.\n     5\u2192slug: /architecture/cqrs-and-event-sourcing\n     6\u2192---\n     7\u2192\n     8\u2192# 03 \u2013 CQRS & Event Sourcing\n     9\u2192\n    10\u2192> \u201cSeparate **what** the system does from **what** the system knows.\u201d  \n    11\u2192> \u2014 EduPay Core Team\n    12\u2192\n    13\u2192EduPay Ledger Academy employs **CQRS** to divide **mutations** (Commands) from **reads** (Queries) so that educators can swap persistence technologies, message buses, or reporting databases without touching domain logic.   \n    14\u2192All state-changing requests are persisted as **immutable domain events**, enabling deterministic replay, powerful audit trails, and student-friendly time-travel debugging.\n    15\u2192\n    16\u2192---\n    17\u2192\n    18\u2192## Table of Contents\n    19\u2192\n    20\u21921. Query Model & Projections  \n    25\u21926. Consistency, Concurrency, and Idempotency  \n    26\u21927. Failure Injection Labs  \n    27\u21928. Further Reading\n    28\u2192\n    29\u2192---\n    30\u2192\n    31\u2192## 1. Domain Vocabulary\n    32\u2192\n    33\u2192Term | Definition\n    34\u2192---- | ----------\n    35\u2192**Command** | An intent _to do_ something. Must either succeed or return an error.\n    36\u2192**Event** | A fact _that something happened_. Can never change or be removed.\n    37\u2192**Aggregate** | A transactional consistency boundary, e.g., `LedgerAccount`.\n    38\u2192**Projection / Read Model** | A denormalized view optimized for reads: dashboards, ledgers, etc.\n    39\u2192\n    40\u2192---\n    41\u2192\n    42\u2192## 2. High Level Flow Diagram\n    43\u2192\n    44\u2192```mermaid\n    45\u2192sequenceDiagram\n    46\u2192    actor Student\n    47\u2192    participant CMD as Command API\n    48\u2192    participant CH as Command Handler\n    49\u2192    participant ES as Event Store (append-only)\n    50\u2192    participant PR as Projector\n    51\u2192    participant RM as Read Model (SQLite)\n    52\u2192    Student->>CMD: POST /accounts/deposit\n    53\u2192    CMD->>CH: DepositFundsCommand\n    54\u2192    CH->>ES: Append(EventDeposited)\n    55\u2192    ES->>PR: Emit(EventDeposited)\n    56\u2192    PR->>RM: UPDATE balances\n    57\u2192    Student->>RM: GET /dashboard\n    58\u2192```\n    59\u2192\n    60\u2192---\n    61\u2192\n    62\u2192## 3. Command Pipeline (Write Model)\n    63\u2192\n    64\u2192Below is a **compile-ready** excerpt (C17) showing how a `CommandBus` validates and dispatches commands to their handlers.  \n    65\u2192It purposefully decouples IO so professors can mock the bus during unit tests.\n    66\u2192\n    67\u2192```c\n    68\u2192/* File: src/cqrs/command_bus.h */\n    69\u2192#ifndef EDU_PAY_COMMAND_BUS_H\n    70\u2192#define EDU_PAY_COMMAND_BUS_H\n    71\u2192\n    72\u2192#include <stdint.h>\n    73\u2192#include <stddef.h>\n    74\u2192#include \"utils/uuid.h\"\n    75\u2192\n    76\u2192/* ---------- Generic Command Definition ---------- */\n    77\u2192typedef struct {\n    78\u2192    uuid_t   id;         /* Correlation ID for tracing */\n    79\u2192    uint64_t timestamp;  /* epoch millis (monotonic)   */\n    80\u2192    const char *type;    /* \"DepositFundsCommand\" etc  */\n    81\u2192    void     *payload;   /* domain-specific struct ptr */\n    82\u2192} command_t;\n    83\u2192\n    84\u2192/* Error codes follow POSIX semantics for reuse in shell scripts */\n    85\u2192typedef enum {\n    86\u2192    CMD_OK          = 0,\n    87\u2192    CMD_ERR_INPUT   = 22,  /* EINVAL */\n    88\u2192    CMD_ERR_HANDLER = 38,  /* ENOSYS */\n    89\u2192    CMD_ERR_REJECT  = 35   /* EDEADLK \u2013 business rule violated */\n    90\u2192} command_status_e;\n    91\u2192\n    92\u2192/* Opaque route handle resolves to specific handler at runtime */\n    93\u2192typedef command_status_e (*command_handler_f)(const command_t *cmd);\n    94\u2192\n    95\u2192/* Register handler */\n    96\u2192int command_bus_register(const char *type, command_handler_f fn);\n    97\u2192\n    98\u2192/* Dispatch (synchronous) */\n    99\u2192command_status_e command_bus_execute(const command_t *cmd);\n   100\u2192\n   101\u2192#endif /* EDU_PAY_COMMAND_BUS_H */\n   102\u2192```\n   103\u2192\n   104\u2192```c\n   105\u2192/* File: src/cqrs/command_bus.c */\n   106\u2192#include \"cqrs/command_bus.h\"\n   107\u2192#include <stdlib.h>\n   108\u2192#include <string.h>\n   109\u2192#include \"utils/hashtable.h\"\n   110\u2192\n   111\u2192/* --- Very light associative table (string \u2192 function ptr) --- */\n   112\u2192static hash_table_t *router = NULL;\n   113\u2192\n   114\u2192int command_bus_register(const char *type, command_handler_f fn) {\n   115\u2192    if (!type || !fn) return -CMD_ERR_INPUT;\n   116\u2192    if (!router) router = ht_create(32);\n   117\u2192    return ht_put(router, type, fn);\n   118\u2192}\n   119\u2192\n   120\u2192command_status_e command_bus_execute(const command_t *cmd) {\n   121\u2192    if (!cmd || !cmd->type) return CMD_ERR_INPUT;\n   122\u2192    command_handler_f fn = ht_get(router, cmd->type);\n   123\u2192    if (!fn) return CMD_ERR_HANDLER;\n   124\u2192    return fn(cmd);\n   125\u2192}\n   126\u2192```\n   127\u2192\n   128\u2192Example Domain Command + Handler:\n   129\u2192\n   130\u2192```c\n   131\u2192/* File: src/payments/commands/deposit_funds.h */\n   132\u2192#ifndef EDU_PAY_COMMAND_DEPOSIT_H\n   133\u2192#define EDU_PAY_COMMAND_DEPOSIT_H\n   134\u2192#include <stdint.h>\n   135\u2192\n   136\u2192typedef struct {\n   137\u2192    char     account_id[36];\n   138\u2192    uint64_t amount_cents;\n   139\u2192    char     currency[4];        /* \"USD\" | \"EUR\" | etc. */\n   140\u2192} deposit_funds_payload_t;\n   141\u2192\n   142\u2192#endif\n   143\u2192```\n   144\u2192\n   145\u2192```c\n   146\u2192/* File:   150\u2192#include \"payments/events/funds_deposited.h\"\n   151\u2192#include \"domain/accounts_repository.h\"\n   152\u2192#include \"utils/clock.h\"\n   153\u2192#include \"utils/currency.h\"\n   154\u2192\n   155\u2192static command_status_e handle_deposit(const command_t *cmd)\n   156\u2192{\n   157\u2192    if (!cmd || !cmd->payload) return CMD_ERR_INPUT;\n   158\u2192    const   162\u2192        return CMD_ERR_REJECT;\n   163\u2192\n   164\u2192    /* Optimistic lock fetch */\n   165\u2192    ledger_account_t acct;\n   166\u2192    if (accounts_repo_load(pl->account_id, &acct) != 0)\n   167\u2192        return CMD_ERR_REJECT; /* Unknown account */\n   168\u2192\n   169\u2192    /* Domain invariants can run here (e.g., AML limits) */\n   170\u2192    /* ... */\n   171\u2192\n   172\u2192    /* --- Produce Event (immutably) --- */\n   173\u2192    funds_deposited_event_t ev = {\n   174\u2192        .base.id        = uuid_v4(),\n   175\u2192        .base.timestamp = clock_epoch_ms(),\n   176\u2192        .base.type      = \"FundsDepositedEvent\",\n   177\u2192        .account_id     = {0},\n   178\u2192        .amount_cents   = 196\u2192```\n   197\u2192\n   198\u2192---\n   199\u2192\n   200\u2192## 4. Event Store Implementation (C)\n   201\u2192\n   202\u2192The **Event Store** is append-only, leverages `mmap(2)` for re-play speed, and stores each record as length-prefixed JSON so that students can grep logs with *jq*.\n   203\u2192\n   204\u2192```c\n   205\u2192/* File: src/event_store/event_store.h */\n   206\u2192#ifndef EDU_PAY_EVENT_STORE_H\n   207\u2192#define EDU_PAY_EVENT_STORE_H\n   208\u2192\n   209\u2192#include <stddef.h>\n   210\u2192#include <stdint.h>\n   211\u2192#include \"events/event.h\"\n   212\u2192\n   213\u2192#define EVT_STORE_OK          0\n   214\u2192#define EVT_STORE_ERR_IO    (-5)\n   215\u2192#define EVT_STORE_ERR_FULL (-28)    /* ENOSPC */\n   216\u2192\n   217\u2192/* Append single event (thread-safe, fsync\u2019ed) */\n   218\u2192int event_store_append(const event_t *ev);\n   219\u2192\n   220\u2192/* Stream all events for replay (blocking). \n   221\u2192   Calls `callback` for each event; stop when it returns non-zero. */\n   222\u2192typedef int (*event_stream_cb)(const event_t *ev, void *ctx);\n   223\u2192int event_store_stream(event_stream_cb callback, void *ctx);\n   224\u2192\n   225\u2192#endif\n   226\u2192```\n   227\u2192\n   228\u2192```c\n   229\u2192/* File: src/event_store/event_store.c */\n   230\u2192#define _POSIX_C_SOURCE 200809L\n   231\u2192#include \"event_store/event_store.h\"\n   232\u2192#include <fcntl.h>\n   233\u2192#include <sys/mman.h>\n   234\u2192#include <sys/stat.h>\n   235\u2192#include <unistd.h>\n   236\u2192#include <pthread.h>\n   237\u2192#include <stdio.h>\n   238\u2192#include <string.h>\n   239\u2192#include \"utils/serialize_json.h\"\n   240\u2192#include \"utils/spinlock.h\"\n   241\u2192\n   242\u2192#define EVENT_STORE_FILE \"./var/event_store.log\"\n   243\u2192#define MAX_EVENT_SIZE   4096   /* hard cap to aid undergrad sanity */\n   244\u2192\n   245\u2192static int fd = -1;\n   246\u2192static pthread_spinlock_t lock;\n   247\u2192\n   248\u2192__attribute__((constructor))\n   249\u2192static void _init_store(void) {\n   250\u2192    fd = open(EVENT_STORE_FILE, O_RDWR | O_CREAT | O_APPEND, 0640);\n   251\u2192    pthread_spin_init(&lock, PTHREAD_PROCESS_PRIVATE);\n   252\u2192}\n   253\u2192\n   254\u2192__attribute__((destructor))\n   255\u2192static void _close_store(void) {\n   256\u2192    if (fd != -1) close(fd);\n   257\u2192    pthread_spin_destroy(&lock);\n   258\u2192}\n   259\u2192\n   260\u2192int event_store_append(const event_t *ev)\n   261\u2192{\n   262\u2192    if (!ev) return EVT_STORE_ERR_IO;\n   263\u2192\n   264\u2192    char buffer[MAX_EVENT_SIZE];\n   265\u2192    ssize_t len = json_serialize_event(ev, buffer, sizeof(buffer));\n   266\u2192    if (len < 0) return EVT_STORE_ERR_IO;\n   267\u2192\n   268\u2192    /* Length-prefixed frame */\n   269\u2192    uint32_t nlen = (uint32_t)len;\n   270\u2192    pthread_spin_lock(&lock);\n   271\u2192    ssize_t w = write(fd, &nlen, sizeof(nlen));\n   272\u2192    w += write(fd, buffer, len);\n   273\u2192    fsync(fd);\n   274\u2192    pthread_spin_unlock(&lock);\n   275\u2192\n   276\u2192    return (w == (ssize_t)(sizeof(nlen) + len)) ? EVT_STORE_OK\n   277\u2192                                                : EVT_STORE_ERR_IO;\n   278\u2192}\n   279\u2192\n   280\u2192int event_store_stream(event_stream_cb cb, void *ctx)\n   281\u2192{\n   282\u2192    if (!cb) return EVT_STORE_ERR_IO;\n   283\u2192\n   284\u2192    int sfd = open(EVENT_STORE_FILE, O_RDONLY);\n   285\u2192    if (sfd < 0) return EVT_STORE_ERR_IO;\n   286\u2192\n   287\u2192    uint32_t nlen;\n   288\u2192    while (read(sfd, &nlen, sizeof(nlen)) == sizeof(nlen)) {\n   289\u2192        if (nlen > MAX_EVENT_SIZE) { close(sfd); return EVT_STORE_ERR_IO; }\n   290\u2192        char buffer[MAX_EVENT_SIZE];\n   291\u2192        if (read(sfd, buffer, nlen) != (ssize_t)nlen) break;\n   292\u2192\n   293\u2192        event_t *ev = json_deserialize_event(buffer, nlen);\n   294\u2192        if (!ev) continue;\n   295\u2192        if (cb(ev, ctx) != 0) { free(ev); break; }\n   296\u2192        free(ev);\n   297\u2192    }\n   298\u2192    close(sfd);\n   299\u2192    return EVT_STORE_OK;\n   300\u2192}\n   301\u2192```\n   302\u2192\n   303\u2192---\n   304\u2192\n   305\u2192## 5. Query Model & Projections\n   306\u2192\n   307\u2192Read models are **eventually consistent**. Every event published above is fanned-out to one or more *Projectors* that transform it into query-optimized databases (SQLite, Redis, CSV for Excel labs).\n   308\u2192\n   309\u2192```c\n   310\u2192/* File: src/projections/balance_projection.c */\n   311\u2192#include \"events/event_bus.h\"\n   312\u2192#include \"payments/events/funds_deposited.h\"\n   313\u2192#include \"database/sqlite.h\"\n   314\u2192\n   315\u2192static int on_funds_deposited(const event_t *ev)\n   316\u2192{\n   317\u2192    const funds_deposited_event_t *e = (const funds_deposited_event_t *)ev;\n   318\u2192    return sqlite_exec(\n   319\u2192        \"INSERT INTO account_balance(account_id, currency, balance_cents) \"\n   320\u2192        \"VALUES (?1, ?2, ?3) \"\n   321\u2192        \"ON CONFLICT(account_id, currency) \"\n   322\u2192        \"DO UPDATE SET balance_cents = balance_cents + excluded.balance_cents;\",\n   323\u2192        e->account_id, e->currency, (int64_t)e->amount_cents);\n   324\u2192}\n   325\u2192\n   326\u2192__attribute__((constructor))\n   327\u2192static void _register_projector(void) {\n   328\u2192    event_bus_subscribe(\"FundsDepositedEvent\", on_funds_deposited);\n   329\u2192}\n   330\u2192```\n   331\u2192\n   332\u2192Students can query via the REST shell or `sqlite3 var/read_models.db`.\n   333\u2192\n   334\u2192---\n   335\u2192\n   336\u2192## 6. Consistency, Concurrency, and Idempotency\n   337\u2192\n   338\u2192\u2022 **Concurrency Control** \u2013 Each aggregate carries a monotonically increasing `version`. Handlers pass the expected `version` into `event_store_append()`.  \n   339\u2192\u2022 **At-Least-Once Delivery** \u2013 Projectors keep an `offset` table so they can re-play events idempotently.  \n   340\u2192\u2022 **Snap-Shots** \u2013 Long-lived aggregates (>2 000 events) periodically persist snapshots to avoid hot-loop rehydration in class.\n   341\u2192\n   342\u2192---\n   343\u2192\n   344\u2192## 7. Failure Injection Labs\n   345\u2192\n   346\u2192Activate with:\n   347\u2192\n   348\u2192```bash\n   349\u2192# Simulate projector downtime\n   350\u2192$ make simulate_projector_outage DURATION=30s\n   351\u2192\n   352\u2192# Induce write-model crash mid-transaction\n   353\u2192$ make chaos_saga MODULE=payments\n   354\u2192```\n   355\u2192\n   356\u2192Students then debug replay & compensating actions per the **Saga Pattern**.\n   357\u2192\n   358\u2192---\n   359\u2192\n   360\u2192## 8. Further Reading\n   361\u2192\n   362\u2192* Greg Young \u2013 *CQRS Journey*  \n   363\u2192* Pat Helland \u2013 *Immutability Changes Everything*  \n   364\u2192* Martin Fowler \u2013 *Event Sourcing*  \n   365\u2192\n   366\u2192---\n   367\u2192\n   368\u2192*\u00a9 2024 EduPay Ledger Academy.*  \n   369\u2192_All code snippets licensed under Apache-2.0 for educational purposes._\n   370\u2192```\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. "     1\u2192```markdown\n     2\u2192# EduPay Ledger Academy  \n     3\u2192### docs/architecture/04_saga_pattern.md\n     4\u2192---\n     5\u2192> Version: 1.3  \n     6\u2192> Last Reviewed: 2024-05-09  \n     7\u2192> Authors: Core Platform Team (@edupay-ledger)  \n     8\u2192> Status: \u2705 Production  \n     9\u2192---\n    10\u2192\n    11\u2192## 1. Why EduPay Uses the Saga Pattern\n    12\u2192\n    13\u2192EduPay processes **millions of distributed, financial micro-transactions** each semester.  \n    14\u2192The platform deliberately avoids *single-phase* database transactions because:\n    15\u2192\n    16\u2192* **Micro-services** compose payments from multiple bounded contexts (Admissions, Bursar, Treasury, FX, Fraud).  \n    17\u2192* **Heterogeneous data stores** (PostgreSQL, Redis, EventStoreDB) participate in a single business flow.  \n    18\u2192* **Resiliency labs** in coursework require controlled failure injection and roll-back.  \n    19\u2192\n    20\u2192A **Saga** slices a long-running business process into a series of *local* ACID transactions plus **compensating steps**.  \n    21\u2192If any step fails, the orchestrator triggers rollback actions in **reverse order**, yielding *eventual consistency* without locking global resources.\n    22\u2192\n    23\u2192```\n    24\u2192Enrollment_Fee \u2192 FX_Conversion \u2192 Treasury_Posting \u2192 Fraud_Scoring \u2192 Receipt_Email\n    25\u2192         \u2502                \u2502                \u2502              \u2502\n    26\u2192         \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n    27\u2192                       Saga Orchestrator (payment_saga.c)       \u2502\n    28\u2192                       \u2022 persists state in Audit_Trail          \u2502\n    29\u2192                       \u2022 broadcasts events over EventBus        \u2502\n    30\u2192                       \u2022 drives rollbacks on failure \u25c4\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n    31\u2192```\n    32\u2192\n    33\u2192---\n    34\u2192\n    35\u2192## 2. High-Level Flow\n    36\u2192\n    37\u21921. **Create** a `payment_saga_t` record in the `audit_trail` stream.  \n    38\u21922. **Send** `SAGA_STEP_BEGIN` for *FX_Conversion* (`fx.c`).  \n    39\u21923. **Local commit** in FX; publish `SAGA_STEP_DONE`.  \n    40\u21924. Orchestrator continues to *Treasury_Posting* (`ledger.c`).  \n    41\u21925. If *Fraud_Scoring* fails, **publish** `SAGA_ABORT`.  \n    42\u21926. Participants receiving `SAGA_ABORT` invoke *compensating* handlers.  \n    43\u21927. Saga ends with `SAGA_ROLLBACK_DONE` or `SAGA_SUCCESS`.\n    44\u2192\n    45\u2192---\n    46\u2192\n    47\u2192## 3. Reference Implementation (C)\n    48\u2192\n    49\u2192All code is kept framework-agnostic, consistent with **Clean Architecture**.  \n    50\u2192Dependencies limited to the standard C library (`pthread` for concurrency).\n    51\u2192\n    52\u2192### 3.1. Public Interface \u2013 `include/saga.h`\n    53\u2192\n    54\u2192```c\n    55\u2192#ifndef EDUPAY_SAGA_H\n    56\u2192#define EDUPAY_SAGA_H\n    57\u2192\n    58\u2192#include <stdint.h>\n    59\u2192#include <stdbool.h>\n    60\u2192\n    61\u2192/* ---------- Event Bus ---------------------------------------------------- */\n    62\u2192\n    63\u2192typedef enum {\n    64\u2192    EVT_SAGA_STEP_BEGIN,\n    65\u2192    EVT_SAGA_STEP_DONE,\n    66\u2192    EVT_SAGA_ABORT,\n    67\u2192    EVT_SAGA_ROLLBACK_DONE,\n    68\u2192    EVT_SAGA_SUCCESS\n    69\u2192} saga_event_type_t;\n    70\u2192\n    71\u2192typedef struct {\n    72\u2192    saga_event_type_t type;\n    73\u2192    uint64_t          saga_id;\n    74\u2192    const char       *step_name;   /* e.g., \"FX_Conversion\" */\n    75\u2192    void             *payload;     /* opaque domain state   */\n    76\u2192} saga_event_t;\n    77\u2192\n    78\u2192/* Subscriber callback signature */\n    79\u2192typedef void (*event_handler_f)(const saga_event_t *evt, void *ctx);\n    80\u2192\n    81\u2192/* Registers a handler; returns 0 on success, -1 on error */\n    82\u2192int eventbus_subscribe(event_handler_f cb, void *ctx);\n    83\u2192\n    84\u2192/* Broadcasts event to all subscribers; thread-safe */\n    85\u2192int eventbus_publish(const saga_event_t *evt);\n    86\u2192\n    87\u2192/* ---------- Saga Orchestrator ------------------------------------------- */\n    88\u2192\n    89\u2192#define SAGA_MAX_STEPS 8\n    90\u2192#define SAGA_STEP_NAME_MAX 32\n    91\u2192\n    92\u2192typedef int (*saga_step_f)(uint64_t saga_id, void **payload);\n    93\u2192typedef int (*saga_comp_f)(uint64_t saga_id, void *payload);\n    94\u2192\n    95\u2192typedef struct {\n    96\u2192    char         name[SAGA_STEP_NAME_MAX];\n    97\u2192    saga_step_f  action;\n    98\u2192    saga_comp_f  compensate;\n    99\u2192} saga_step_def_t;\n   100\u2192\n   101\u2192typedef struct {\n   102\u2192    uint64_t        id;\n   103\u2192    uint8_t         step_count;\n   104\u2192    uint8_t         current;\n   105\u2192    saga_step_def_t steps[SAGA_MAX_STEPS];\n   106\u2192    bool            aborted;\n   107\u2192} payment_saga_t;\n   108\u2192\n   109\u2192/* Initializes a saga with the supplied steps */\n   110\u2192void saga_init(payment_saga_t *saga, uint64_t id,\n   111\u2192               const saga_step_def_t *steps,\n   112\u2192               uint8_t step_count);\n   113\u2192\n   114\u2192/* Executes saga synchronously; returns 0 on success, -1 on failure */\n   115\u2192int saga_execute(payment_saga_t *saga);\n   116\u2192\n   117\u2192#endif /* EDUPAY_SAGA_H */\n   118\u2192```\n   119\u2192\n   120\u2192### 3.2. Core Implementation \u2013 `src/saga.c`\n   121\u2192\n   122\u2192```c\n   123\u2192#include \"saga.h\"\n   124\u2192#include <pthread.h>\n   125\u2192#include <stdio.h>\n   126\u2192#include <stdlib.h>\n   127\u2192#include <string.h>\n   128\u2192\n   129\u2192#define BUS_MAX_HANDLERS 16\n   130\u2192\n   131\u2192/* ----------------- Simple In-Process Event Bus -------------------------- */\n   132\u2192\n   133\u2192typedef struct {\n   134\u2192    event_handler_f cb;\n   135\u2192    void           *ctx;\n   136\u2192} handler_entry_t;\n   137\u2192\n   138\u2192static handler_entry_t BUS[BUS_MAX_HANDLERS];\n   139\u2192static pthread_mutex_t BUS_LOCK = PTHREAD_MUTEX_INITIALIZER;\n   140\u2192\n   141\u2192int eventbus_subscribe(event_handler_f cb, void *ctx)\n   142\u2192{\n   143\u2192    pthread_mutex_lock(&BUS_LOCK);\n   144\u2192    for (int i = 0; i < BUS_MAX_HANDLERS; ++i) {\n   145\u2192        if (BUS[i].cb == NULL) {\n   146\u2192            BUS[i].cb  = cb;\n   147\u2192            BUS[i].ctx = ctx;\n   148\u2192            pthread_mutex_unlock(&BUS_LOCK);\n   149\u2192            return 0;\n   150\u2192        }\n   151\u2192    }\n   152\u2192    pthread_mutex_unlock(&BUS_LOCK);\n   153\u2192    return -1; /* No slots */\n   154\u2192}\n   155\u2192\n   156\u2192int eventbus_publish(const saga_event_t *evt)\n   157\u2192{\n   158\u2192    pthread_mutex_lock(&BUS_LOCK);\n   159\u2192    handler_entry_t handlers[BUS_MAX_HANDLERS];\n   160\u2192    memcpy(handlers, BUS, sizeof(handlers));\n   161\u2192    pthread_mutex_unlock(&BUS_LOCK);\n   162\u2192\n   163\u2192    for (int i = 0; i < BUS_MAX_HANDLERS; ++i) {\n   164\u2192        if (handlers[i].cb)\n   165\u2192            handlers[i].cb(evt, handlers[i].ctx);\n   166\u2192    }\n   167\u2192    return 0;\n   168\u2192}\n   169\u2192\n   170\u2192/* ----------------- Saga Orchestration ---------------------------------- */\n   171\u2192\n   172\u2192static void publish_step_event(saga_event_type_t type,\n   173\u2192                               const payment_saga_t *saga,\n   174\u2192                               const char *step_name,\n   175\u2192                               void *payload)\n   176\u2192{\n   177\u2192    saga_event_t evt = {\n   178\u2192        .type      = type,\n   179\u2192        .saga_id   = saga->id,\n   180\u2192        .step_name = step_name,\n   181\u2192        .payload   = payload\n   182\u2192    };\n   183\u2192    eventbus_publish(&evt);\n   184\u2192}\n   185\u2192\n   186\u2192void saga_init(payment_saga_t *s, uint64_t id,\n   187\u2192               const saga_step_def_t *steps,\n   188\u2192               uint8_t step_count)\n   189\u2192{\n   190\u2192    memset(s, 0, sizeof(*s));\n   191\u2192    s->id         = id;\n   192\u2192    s->step_count = step_count > SAGA_MAX_STEPS ? SAGA_MAX_STEPS : step_count;\n   193\u2192    memcpy(s->steps, steps, s->step_count * sizeof(saga_step_def_t));\n   194\u2192}\n   195\u2192\n   196\u2192static int rollback(payment_saga_t *saga)\n   197\u2192{\n   198\u2192    for (int i = saga->current; i >= 0; --i) {\n   199\u2192        saga_step_def_t *step = &saga->steps[i];\n   200\u2192        if (step->compensate) {\n   201\u2192            publish_step_event(EVT_SAGA_ABORT, saga, step->name, NULL);\n   202\u2192            if (step->compensate(saga->id, NULL) != 0)\n   203\u2192                fprintf(stderr, \"\u26a0  Compensation failed at %s\\n\", step->name);\n   204\u2192        }\n   205\u2192    }\n   206\u2192    saga_event_t done = {\n   207\u2192        .type      = EVT_SAGA_ROLLBACK_DONE,\n   208\u2192        .saga_id   = saga->id,\n   209\u2192        .step_name = \"ROLLBACK\"\n   210\u2192    };\n   211\u2192    eventbus_publish(&done);\n   212\u2192    return -1;\n   213\u2192}\n   214\u2192\n   215\u2192int saga_execute(payment_saga_t *saga)\n   216\u2192{\n   217\u2192    for (saga->current = 0; saga->current < saga->step_count; ++saga->current) {\n   218\u2192        saga_step_def_t *step = &saga->steps[saga->current];\n   219\u2192\n   220\u2192        publish_step_event(EVT_SAGA_STEP_BEGIN, saga, step->name, NULL);\n   221\u2192\n   222\u2192        void *payload = NULL;\n   223\u2192        if (step->action(saga->id, &payload) != 0) {\n   224\u2192            fprintf(stderr, \"\u274c  Saga %lu failed at step %s\\n\",\n   225\u2192                    saga->id, step->name);\n   226\u2192            saga->aborted = true;\n   227\u2192            return rollback(saga);\n   228\u2192        }\n   229\u2192\n   230\u2192        publish_step_event(EVT_SAGA_STEP_DONE, saga, step->name, payload);\n   231\u2192    }\n   232\u2192\n   233\u2192    saga_event_t ok = {\n   234\u2192        .type      = EVT_SAGA_SUCCESS,\n   235\u2192        .saga_id   = saga->id,\n   236\u2192        .step_name = \"COMPLETED\"\n   237\u2192    };\n   238\u2192    eventbus_publish(&ok);\n   239\u2192    return 0;\n   240\u2192}\n   241\u2192```\n   242\u2192\n   243\u2192### 3.3. Example Steps \u2013 `src/steps_fx.c`, `src/steps_ledger.c`\n   244\u2192\n   245\u2192```c\n   246\u2192/* src/steps_fx.c */\n   247\u2192#include \"saga.h\"\n   248\u2192#include <stdio.h>\n   249\u2192\n   250\u2192int fx_convert(uint64_t id, void **payload)\n   251\u2192{\n   252\u2192    (void)payload; /* Not needed for demo */\n   253\u2192    printf(\"\ud83d\udcb1  FX_Conversion performed for saga %lu\\n\", id);\n   254\u2192    /* simulate success */\n   255\u2192    return 0;\n   256\u2192}\n   257\u2192\n   258\u2192int fx_reverse(uint64_t id, void *payload)\n   259\u2192{\n   260\u2192    (void)payload;\n   261\u2192    printf(\"\u21a9  FX_Conversion reversed for saga %lu\\n\", id);\n   262\u2192    return 0;\n   263\u2192}\n   264\u2192```\n   265\u2192\n   266\u2192```c\n   267\u2192/* src/steps_ledger.c */\n   268\u2192#include \"saga.h\"\n   269\u2192#include <stdio.h>\n   270\u2192\n   271\u2192int ledger_post(uint64_t id, void **payload)\n   272\u2192{\n   273\u2192    (void)payload;\n   274\u2192    printf(\"\ud83d\udcd2  Ledger posting OK for saga %lu\\n\", id);\n   275\u2192    return 0;\n   276\u2192}\n   277\u2192\n   278\u2192int ledger_reverse(uint64_t id, void *payload)\n   279\u2192{\n   280\u2192    (void)payload;\n   281\u2192    printf(\"\u21a9  Ledger posting reversed for saga %lu\\n\", id);\n   282\u2192    return 0;\n   283\u2192}\n   284\u2192```\n   285\u2192\n   286\u2192### 3.4. Demonstration Driver \u2013 `samples/payment_saga.c`\n   287\u2192\n   288\u2192```c\n   289\u2192#include \"saga.h\"\n   290\u2192#include <stdio.h>\n   291\u2192#include <stdlib.h>\n   292\u2192#include <time.h>\n   293\u2192\n   294\u2192/* ---------- Step Implementations --------------------------------------- */\n   295\u2192extern int fx_convert(uint64_t, void **);\n   296\u2192extern int fx_reverse(uint64_t, void *);\n   297\u2192\n   298\u2192extern int ledger_post(uint64_t, void **);\n   299\u2192extern int ledger_reverse(uint64_t, void *);\n   300\u2192\n   301\u2192static int fraud_score(uint64_t id, void **payload)\n   302\u2192{\n   303\u2192    (void)payload;\n   304\u2192    printf(\"\ud83d\udd75  Fraud scoring started for saga %lu\\n\", id);\n   305\u2192\n   306\u2192    /* Simulate 30% failure rate for classroom chaos monkeys */\n   307\u2192    if (rand() % 10 < 3) {\n   308\u2192        fprintf(stderr, \"\ud83d\udea8  Fraud scoring FAILED (suspicious)\\n\");\n   309\u2192        return -1;\n   310\u2192    }\n   311\u2192\n   312\u2192    printf(\"\u2705  Fraud scoring passed\\n\");\n   313\u2192    return 0;\n   314\u2192}\n 338\u2192\n   339\u2192    saga_step_def_t steps[] = {\n   340\u2192        { \"FX_Conversion\",   fx_convert,   fx_reverse   },\n   341\u2192        { \"Ledger_Posting\",  ledger_post,  ledger_reverse },\n   342\u2192        { \"Fraud_Scoring\",   fraud_score,  fraud_reverse }\n   343\u2192    };\n   344\u2192\n   345\u2192    payment_saga_t saga;\n   346\u2192    saga_init(&saga, 42, steps, 3);\n   347\u2192\n   348\u2192    int rc = saga_execute(&saga);\n   349\u2192    printf(rc == 0 ? \"\ud83c\udf89  Saga completed successfully!\\n\"\n   350\u2192                   : \"\ud83d\udc94  Saga rolled back.\\n\");\n   351\u2192    return rc;\n   352\u2192}\n   353\u2192```\n   354\u2192\n   355\u2192Compile & Run:\n   356\u2192\n   357\u2192```bash\n   358\u2192gcc
